      <foreign lang="ar"> <ref cref="n38360-1" target="استمرّ" n="1" type="1" subtype="WO" lang="ar" select="n38366"/></foreign>. (S, A, Mgh, K.) You say, <foreign lang="ar">مَرَّ الرَّجُلُ</foreign>, (TK,) and <foreign lang="ar">الدَّهْرُ</foreign>, (Msb,) and <foreign lang="ar">الأَمْرُ</foreign>; and  
      <foreign lang="ar"> <ref cref="n38360-2" target="استمرّ" n="2" type="1" subtype="WO" lang="ar" select="n38366"/></foreign>; (A, Mgh;) <hi rend="ital">The man,</hi> (TK,) and <hi rend="ital">time,</hi> (Msb,) and <hi rend="ital">the affair,</hi> (A, Mgh,) <hi rend="ital">passed;</hi> &amp;c. (A, Mgh, Msb, TK.) The saying in the Kur, [vii. 189,] <foreign lang="ar">حَمَلَتْ حَمْلًا خَفِيفًا فَمَرَّتْ بِهِ</foreign> signifies <hi rend="ital">i. q.</hi><foreign lang="ar"> <ref cref="n38360-3" target="استمرّت" n="3" type="5" subtype="TFSO" lang="ar"/>به</foreign>, (A, K,) which is another reading, (Bd,) i. e., [<hi rend="ital">She bore a light burden</hi> in her womb, <hi rend="ital">and</hi>] <hi rend="ital">went with it, and moved from place to place, and rose and sat,</hi> not being oppressed by its weight: (A:) [or <hi rend="ital">went on with it in the same course</hi> or <hi rend="ital">manner:</hi>] or <hi rend="ital">went and came with it,</hi> by reason of its lightness: (Jel:) or <hi rend="ital">rose and sat with it,</hi> (Zj, Bd,) not being oppressed by its weight: (Zj:) so accord. to both the readings mentioned above: (Bd:) by the burden being meant the impregnating fluid. (Bd, Jel, TA.)          <sense type="b" n="2">-b2-</sense>  [It is also said of water, meaning <hi rend="ital">It ran,</hi> or <hi rend="ital">flowed.</hi> And one says, <foreign lang="ar">مَرَّتِ الرِّيحُ</foreign>
                  <hi rend="ital">The wind passed along,</hi> or <hi rend="ital">blew.</hi>]          <sense type="b" n="3">-b3-</sense>  <foreign lang="ar">مَرَّ بِهِ</foreign>, (S, M, A, Msb, K,) and <foreign lang="ar">مَرَّ عَلَيْهِ</foreign>, (S, A, Msb,) but the former is more common than the latter, (Mughnee, voce <foreign lang="ar">بِ</foreign>,) for which the BenooYarbooa say, <foreign lang="ar">مِرَّ عليه</foreign>, with kesr, (TA,) and <foreign lang="ar">مَرَّهُ</foreign>, [respecting which see what follows the explanation,] (M, K,) aor.

                     <orth orig="Bu" lang="ar" marker="maru3a">مَرُرَ</orth>
                  </form>, (S,) inf. n. <foreign lang="ar">مَرٌّ</foreign> and <foreign lang="ar">مَمَرٌّ</foreign> (S, A, Msb) and <foreign lang="ar">مُرُورٌ</foreign>; (A, Msb;) and <foreign lang="ar"> <ref cref="n38360-4" target="اِمْتَرَّ" n="4" type="5" subtype="FSO" lang="ar"/>بِهِ</foreign>, and <foreign lang="ar">اِمْتَرَّ عَلَيْهِ</foreign>; (M, K;) <hi rend="ital">He passed,</hi> or <hi rend="ital">went, by him,</hi> or <hi rend="ital">it;</hi> syn. <foreign lang="ar">اِجْتَازَ</foreign>, (S, Msb,) or <foreign lang="ar">جَازَ عَلَيْهِ</foreign>, (M, K,) or <foreign lang="ar">جَاوَزَهُ وَذَهَبَ</foreign>. (A.) <foreign lang="ar">مَرَّ</foreign> may be a verb trans. by means of a particle and without a particle: or in <foreign lang="ar">مَرَّهُ</foreign> the particle may be suppressed: Jereer says, <quote>
                     <L>
                        <foreign lang="ar">تَمُرُّونَ الدِّيَارَ وَلَمْ تَعُوجُوا</foreign>
                     </L>
                     <L>
                        <foreign lang="ar">كَلَامُكُمُ عَلَىَّ إِذًا حَرَامُ</foreign>
                     </L>
                  </quote> [<hi rend="ital">Ye pass by the dwellings without turning aside and alighting: the speaking to you is therefore forbidden to me</hi>]: but it is said that the true reading is <foreign lang="ar">مَرَرْتُمْ بِالدِّيَارِ</foreign> [<hi rend="ital">Ye have passed by the dwellings</hi>]: which shows that he feared to make the verb trans. without a particle: IAar says, that <foreign lang="ar">مَرَّ زَيْدًا</foreign> signifies the same as <foreign lang="ar">مَرَّ بِهِ</foreign> [<hi rend="ital">He passed by Zeyd</hi>], without being elliptical, but as being properly trans.; but IJ, allowing this, says that it is not a phrase commonly obtaining. (M, TA.)          <sense type="b" n="4">-b4-</sense>  [<foreign lang="ar">مَرَّ عَلَيْهِ</foreign> also signifies <hi rend="ital">He,</hi> or <hi rend="ital">it, passed,</hi> or <hi rend="ital">went, along,</hi> or <hi rend="ital">over,</hi> or <hi rend="ital">across, it.</hi> You say, <foreign lang="ar">مَرَّ عَلَى الجِسْرِ</foreign>
                  <hi rend="ital">He passed,</hi> or <hi rend="ital">went,</hi>
                  <pb n="2700"/>
                  <hi rend="ital">along,</hi> or <hi rend="ital">over the bridge,</hi> or <hi rend="ital">dyke.</hi>] And <foreign lang="ar">مَرَّ</foreign>
                  <foreign lang="ar">السِّكِّينُ عَلَى حَلْقِ الشَّاةِ</foreign>
                  <hi rend="ital">The knife passed across the throat of the sheep,</hi> or <hi rend="ital">goat.</hi> (Msb.)          <sense type="b" n="5">-b5-</sense>  [Also, <hi rend="ital">It</hi> (a period of time) <hi rend="ital">passed over him,</hi> or <hi rend="ital">it:</hi> and <hi rend="ital">it</hi> (a calamity) <hi rend="ital">came upon him:</hi> see an ex. of the latter signification below, voce <foreign lang="ar">مُرٌّ</foreign>.]          <sense type="b" n="6">-b6-</sense>  <foreign lang="ar">مَرَّ بِهِ</foreign> as syn. with  
      <foreign lang="ar"> <ref cref="n38360-5" target="أَمَرَّهُ" n="5" type="1" subtype="WO" lang="ar"/></foreign>, trans. of <foreign lang="ar">مَرَّ</foreign>: see 4.       <sense type="A" n="2">-A2-</sense>  <foreign lang="ar">مَرَّ</foreign>, aor.
